O ! Bikshus and scholars,
You should thoroughly examine my words
Like examining gold by burning, cutting and rubbing,
Then adopt them but not out of respect for me.

A Garland of Pearls
Prologue
The major and minor marks of the extraordinarily excellent body
shine
The dharma-sound of the sixty qualities of excellent speech
pervades
The excellent mind which is profound and free from elaborations
glorifies with compassion
I bow down to the incomparable excellent guide, the Lion of the
Shakyas.
In the isle of the stainless and perfectly milky lake
The emanation body was born from a fragrant lotus stem
Whoever finds the treasure of thoughts of the stainless truth body
May the gracious Lake-born Vajra always protect.
The principal sons of Buddha: Manjushri, Vajrapani,
Avalokiteshvara,
Nagarjuna, Asanga, Shantirakshita, Bairocana, Ka-chog-zhang,
The Three Omniscient masters,? Jigme Choekyi Wangpo and so on
To the assembly of these gracious direct and indirect lamas I bow
down wholeheartedly.
The three emanations of the three families,
Thonmi Sambhota the only eye of the Land of Snow,
Gongpa Rabsel and Ma-yo-tsang
I often think of you as the Land of Snow is grateful to you.

A Garland of Pearls
The real Manjushri, an emanation of the wisdom of all the
buddhas,
Who was more gracious than all the buddhas
And who elucidated Buddhadharma in samsara and nirvana with
bodhisattva deeds
May Mipham Lama be glorified.
The holder of the treasure of sublime scriptural and realized dharma
Whose mind is impartial and free from prejudices
Whose treasure of compassion is perfected in benefiting others
I prostrate to Mahasiddha Choekyi Gyalpo' with my crown.
Commencing with these praises to these superiors beings, I will explain
the meaning of the precious Buddhadharma the source of benefit for
all sentient beings in the first chapter. In the second chapter, I will
explain, in brief, how the teachings of sutra and tantra came into
being in India. In the third chapter, I will briefly explain how it spread
in Tibet. In the fourth chapter, I will briefly explain the history of
Tolag Nenang Monastery. In the fifth chapter, in a few words, I will
explain the benefits of Avalokiteshvara's six-syllable mantra. And in
the sixth chapter, I will explain the benefits of prostrations and
circumambulations.

A Garland of Pearls
Buddhadharma
What does Buddhadharma mean? How should one practice it? One
should not practice it without proper knowledge and analysis. It is so
because the Buddha said:
O ! Bikshus and scholars,
You should thoroughly examine my words
Like examining gold by burning, cutting and rubbing,
Then adopt them but not out of respect for me.
The Buddha also said:
I have shown you the way to liberation
But you should know that liberation is in your hands.
What Buddha showed to sentient beings was the method of achieving
the state of omniscience and liberation from samsara by realizing the
true nature of the Four Noble Truths. You can protect yourself from
the suffering that you experience through the insight that realizes
emptiness, which is the antidote of self-grasping the root cause of the
three afflictive emotions: attachment, hatred and ignorance.
From the words of Jetsun Milarepa:
In general, the Buddha gave teachings
In order to overcome worldly concerns.
Don't you think contemporary people conceited about
being scholars
Have increased their eight worldly concerns?
5

A Garland of Pearls
Bodhisattva Ngulchu Thogmey Sangpo said with regard to what
Buddhadharma means:
If you do not analyze your own faults
You might do non-dharma deeds by putting on the
appearance of a practitioner
Hence, you should always examine your faults
And discard them ; this is the practice of bodhisattvas.
If you practice dharma just as he said, then you will become a genuine
dharma practitioner.
How should one practice dharma? In the words of the Buddha:
Never commit any wrong-doing,
Practice virtuous deeds perfectly,
And tame your mind completely,
This is the Buddhadharma.
Let me briefly explain this quintessential instruction. The first line
“Never commit any wrong-doing," means you should earnestly
abandon the ten non-virtuous actions.
These are the three non-virtuous actions of body. (1) Killing:
Taking even the life of an insect under the influence of afflictive
emotions such as hatred, (2) Stealing: The acts of stealing are robbing
by force, taking without notifying the owner and taking what is
not given and (3) Sexual misconduct: The acts of indulging in
adultery and sexual misconduct, such as copulating at inappropriate
times and places.
These are the four non-virtuous actions of speech . (1) Lying:
The act of lying with the thought of deceiving others, (2) Divisive
Speech: Speaking divisively to separate two or more friendly people
and causing disharmony between them either directly or indirectly,
(3) Offensive Speech : This is speaking any word, pleasant or
unpleasant, that disturbs the mind of others, and (4) Idle Gossiping:
It is speaking meaningless and worthless words.
These are the three non-virtuous actions of mind. (1)
Covetousness: It is an emotional feeling strongly desiring someone's

A Garland of Pearls
wealth, etc. to become your own, and thinking, “May it become
mine." (2) Malice: Out of hatred, thinking, “May I harm him or
her,” and focusing on someone's good things, out of jealousy,
thinking, “I wish he or she didn't have such good things.” (3)
Wrong Views: Due to ignorance, holding views such as denying
the existence of the law of causality and past and future lives.
In short, you should earnestly refrain from the ten non-virtuous
actions of body, speech and mind.
The second line “Practice virtuous deeds perfectly” means you
should not only abstain from the ten non-virtuous actions, but
also practice the ten virtuous actions meticulously. The three
virtuous actions of body are as follows. You should not only avoid
killing, but you should put effort into the methods used for
protecting those suffering from the fear of being killed. You should
not only avoid taking what is not given, but you should practice
giving as much as you can. And you should not only stop indulging
in adultery, but you should be content with the act of copulation.
The four virtuous actions of speech are as follows. You should
not only refrain from telling lies, but you should tell the truth.
You should not only refrain from speaking offensive words, but
you should speak pleasant words. You should not only refrain from
divisive speech, but you should speak words that create harmony.
And you should not only refrain from idle gossiping, but you should
speak words which have meaning.
The three virtuous actions of mind are as follows. You should
not only refrain from generating covetousness, but you should be
contented with your possessions. You should not only refrain from
malice, but you should also generate an altruistic attitude. You
should not only refrain from generating wrong views, but you
should hold correct views with regard to the teachings of the
Buddha, such as the teachings on the existence of the law of
causality and past and future lives.
In short, you should practice the ten virtuous actions with a
perfect mental attitude.

A Garland of Pearls
The meaning of the third line “ Tame your mind completely”
is: Buddhadharma should be primarily practiced within your own
mind. If you hold afflictive emotions such as covetousness, malice
and wrong views within, then even if you look like a practitioner,
it is one of the worst infringements of dharma and the heaviest
wrong-doings. It is so because the Buddha said in various sutras
and tantras:
On account of virtuous or non-virtuous thoughts
Deeds become wholesome or unwholesome
And not by the size of their appearance.
From the words of the omniscient Longchen Rabjampa:
By collecting huge taxes from the poor and destitute,
For the sake of amassing virtuous actions for oneself,
By building huge objects of worship and displaying
extensive offerings etc.,
These are the causes of accumulating unwholesome
deeds for others.
To have a virtuous mind is my heartfelt advice.
Lord Tsongkhapa said :
If the motivation is good, even the ground and path
become noble,
If the motivation is bad, even the ground and path
become corrupt,
Since everything depends upon the motivation,
One should always make effort to generate a good
motivation.
Likewise, Lord Nagarjuna also said:
Attachment, hatred and ignorance are the three
From which actions generated are non-virtuous,
Non-attachment, non-hatred and non-ignorance are
the three
From which actions generated are virtuous.

A Garland of Pearls
In short, not taking into consideration the actions of your body
and speech as primary and protecting your mind from generating
afflictive emotions such as attachment, hatred, ignorance, conceit,
jealousy and rivalry is the meaning of the third line, “ Tame your
mind completely”.
The fourth line " This is the Buddhadharma” means, as stated above,
that this is the practice: you should never commit any wrong-doing,
you should practice virtuous deeds perfectly and after taming your
mind completely, you should not incite afflictive emotions within
other sentient beings.

A Garland of Pearls
The Spread of Buddhism in India
I will briefly explain how the doctrine of sutra and tantra came into
India. The Garland of Oral Transmission of Hearing Lineages states:
When buddhas come to this world
In the great teachings of theirs,
It is possible that big controversies may arise,
Hence, firstly narrate the annals of how dharma came
into existence.
As stated, let me first briefly narrate how the sublime
Buddhadharma spread in the noble land of India. The Perfectly
Arraying the Virtues Sutra states:
From the moment when I first generated bodhichitta, I
accumulated merit for three great incalculable eons.
Beholding the blind and guideless sentient beings whose
lifespan is of a hundred years, I have attained the state
of Buddhahood in this world of Jambudvipa and I
thoroughly turned the inconceivable Wheel of
Dharma...
In some of the tantric texts, it is similarly explained. However, the
difference is as follows. While the Buddha was abiding in the
immovable meditative stabilization (samadhi) by the soothing
Nairanjana River that flows in the vicinity of Bodhgaya, the buddhas
of the ten directions assembled and aroused him from that samadhi.
While his physical body stayed on the bank of the same Nairanjana
River, his wisdom body proceeded to the pure land of Akanishtha
11

A Garland of Pearls
Ghanavyuha. All the buddhas of the ten directions conferred upon
him empowerments. There he became a buddha through the
contemplation in sequence of the five abhisambodhis. Afterwards, at
Vajra Seat (Bodhgaya) he demonstrated the method of attaining
Buddhahood. It is so because Acharya Aryadeva said:
The mode of attaining enlightenment
Is said to be of two: the outer and the inner.
The uncommon assertion of the Mahayana school of thought is
that after attaining Buddhahood in Akanishtha Ghanavyuha, the
densely arrayed heaven , he demonstrated the method of attaining
Buddhahood at Vajra Seat, just as is said in the Sutra of Descent to
Lanka (Lankavatara):9
Beyond the heaven of the Pure Abode
Lies the fascinating Akanishtha Heaven
Where the perfect Buddha attained Buddhahood
And an emanation attains Buddhahood here in this
world.
Amongst the many assertions mentioned above, here I will explain
the assertion shared with the Theravadin tradition. Our
compassionate and skillful teacher, Buddha Shakyamuni, generated
the mind of enlightenment (bodhichitta) in front of the Buddha
Mahamuni for three incalculable eons. Then , while still on the
path of accumulation, he finished amassing the two accumulations.
When the lifespan of humans was twenty-thousand years, Buddha
Kashyapa arrived in this world. At that time, Buddha Shakyamuni
took birth as a youthful brahman. In the next life, he took rebirth
in Tushita Heaven as the son of a god called Dampa Togkarpo and
gave dharma teachings to the gods. Once again, in order to guide
sentient beings to happiness, he demonstrated the twelve deeds in
the billion-fold universe. For example, when the human lifespan
became a hundred years, he checked the lineage, location, father,
mother and time and before leaving Tushita, he gave teachings to
the gods on how to purify the dying process.
12

A Garland of Pearls
Then he demonstrated the deed of descending from Tushita in
the form of a white elephant with six tusks. When Queen Maya was
observing the posadha fast, he entered her womb from the right side
of her lungs and blessed her womb as a celestial palace on the full
moon day of the sixth month of the Female-Earth-Sheep year [of
the Tibetan calendar). In the celestial palace, he gave teachings to the
gods and humans on how to purify the birthplace.
On the 7th day of the fourth month of the Iron-Monkey year,
the Buddha demonstrated the deed of rebirth in the Lumbini
Garden . When Queen Maya was holding a branch of a fig tree, the
child came out of her ribs wearing clothes. The child walked seven
steps in each of the four cardinal directions while saying, “... I am
the highest in this universe.” His birth was also celebrated by the
celestial beings with praises. Thus, with numerous marvelous signs,
he demonstrated the deed of his birth .
He then displayed the deed of showing his skills in the worldly
arts. From individual masters, he learned reading and writing,
archery and other physical and verbal skills and became expert in
all the arts.
Then he demonstrated his deed of enjoyment of the circle of
noble women such as Yashodhara, Sa-tso-ma and Drak-zin -ma
along with sixty thousand subjects.
At the age of twenty-nine, he demonstrated by vowing to
generate the thought of renunciation after seeing the four currents
of birth, aging, sickness and death. Then the Four Great Kings
lifted him into the sky towards the Pure Stupa where he renounced
the world by cutting his own hair.
Following that, by the river Nairanjana, he entered into the 'Space
Filling' meditative stabilization, and practiced asceticism for six years.
When he reached the age of thirty-five, on the full moon day of
the fourth month of the Wood-Horse year, while sitting on a cushion
of grasses under a Bodhi-tree, he made a firm vow stating:
I shall not release myself from this cross-legged
posture,
Until I attain the state of uncontamination.
13

A Garland of Pearls
After defeating countless demons in battle through the meditative
stabilization of loving kindness, he realized the unborn wisdom
and attained Buddhahood. When he attained the state of complete
enlightenment, the earth trembled and infinite rays of light
appeared. Seeing these omens, the celestial beings praised him .
After the Buddha had exhibited the method of attaining
Buddhahood under the Bodhi-tree, he pronounced:
I have found a nectar-like dharma
Which is profound, peaceful, free from elaborations,
luminous and uncompounded.
Whoever I teach will not comprehend it,
Hence, I will abide in the woods.
When the Buddha remained silent without teaching for seven weeks,
Brahma and Indra appeared before him and they pleaded with
him to turn the Wheel of Dharma. It was said that the acceptance
of their plea by the Buddha was heard even in the Akanishtha
Heaven.
Although the Buddha turned three successive Wheels of
Dharma, let us discuss here the chief topic of discussion the five
perfect aspects of the First Turning of the Wheel of Dharma. The
five perfect aspects are: (1) The Perfect Teacher is the Lord Buddha,
(2) the Perfect Place is Deer Park Rsipatana, where five hundred
Pratyekabuddhas burned their bodies, and the ashes and relics fell
to the earth, (3) the Perfect Time is the fourth day of the sixth
month, (4) the Perfect Teaching is the Four Noble Truths, (5) the
Perfect Retinue is the Five Noble Disciples (Pancaka Bhadravargiya):
Ajnatakaundinya, Ashvajit, Vaspa, Mahanama and Bhadrika, and
the eighty thousand celestial beings. The Five Noble Disciples
attained the state of Foe-destroyer (Arhat) and the eighty thousand
celestial beings saw the truth.
At the age of eighty-one, the Buddha decided to pass into the
expanse of peace after entrusting to Mahakashyapa the responsibility
of his teachings, along with the four-fold disciples.10 Then he
demonstrated the method of passing into the expanse of peace
14

A Garland of Pearls
under a Sala tree in the city of Kushinagara on the full moon day of
the fourth month of the Iron-Dragon year.
The seven successors of the Buddha are clearly mentioned in
the Vinaya Agama.11 The foremost successor was Mahakashyapa,
to whom the Buddha entrusted half of his teachings and appointed
as his regent. Not long after the Buddha attained the state of
complete enlightenment, Mahakashyapa went to meet him while
the Buddha was residing near the Bumang stupa called. Right
after seeing the Buddha, Kashyapa generated faith within and
uttered, “Bhagavan! You are my Teacher and I am your disciple,"
three times. After which the Buddha responded, “I am your Teacher
and you are my disciple.” Kashyapa then received the full ordination
of a monk. Later he became well-versed in the teachings of the
Buddha, and was well respected by the followers.
Mahakashyapa headed the First Council, then he entrusted
the responsibility to Ananda and decided to pass into Nirvana. He
then went to the land of the Nagas to prostrate to the Buddha's
tooth and returned to the mountain Kukkutapada (Riwo
Jakangchen), he blessed his body (his corpse) so that it would not
decay until Lord Maitreya came into the world. Then he passed
into Nirvana.
The responsibility was entrusted in succession from Ananda
to Arya Shanavasa, Arya Upagupta, Arya Dhitika, Arya Kala and
Arya Mahasudarsana. Thus, the seven successors of the Buddha took
great care of the teachings of the Buddha.
Shortly after the period of King Mahapadma, Chandrarakshita
became the King of Odivisar. It is said that Arya Manjushri came to
his house in the guise of a bhikshu, preached some Mahayana teachings
and left a volume of scripture. It was the Eighty Thousand Verses of
Prajnaparamita. This was said to be the first appearance of the
Mahayana in the human world after the Buddha passed into Nirvana.
Around this time, in Kashmir, there was a bhikshu called Sanjaya
who taught the Tripitaka extensively and raised many spiritual masters
of the Vaibhashika and Sautrantika schools such as Dharmatrata and
Sthavra.
15

A Garland of Pearls
After that Mahasathavira Nanda, who was born in Anga, became
well-versed in Mahayana teachings. At the same time there appeared
innumerable spiritual masters in different places capable of preaching
the Mahayana teachings such as Avitarka, Vigataragadvaja and
Jnanatala. There were about five hundred preachers of the Mahayana
teachings who attained the samadhi called 'the Stream of Dharma'.
As a result, they listened to the Mahayana teachings from Maitreya,
Manjushri, Avalokiteshvara, Guhyapati and so on. From the land of
gods, Nagas, Gandharvas, Rakshasas, etc. especially from the land
of Nagas most of the sutras were obtained, like the Jewel Mound
Sutra (Arya-ratnakuta), Huge Collection of Sutras (Avatamsaka Sutra),
Sutra of Descent to Lanka (Lankavatara), Dense Array of Adornments
Sutra (Gandavyuha) and Compendium of the Dharmas Sutra (Dharmasamgiti).
With the help of supra-mundane deities such as Maitreya,
Manjushri, Avalokiteshvara and Guhyapati the system of the Middle
Way School was elucidated for the first time.
About this time, there appeared many spiritual masters of
Vaibhashika and Sautrantika schools such as Buddhadeva, of
Vaibhashika, in the city of Varanasi and Shrilabha of Sautrantika,
in Kashmir. Dharmatrata, Ghosaka, Vasumitra and Buddhadeva
were famed as the four great Vaibhashika masters and it is said that
each of them had a hundred thousand disciples.
After that, Acharya Nagarjuna was born in Vidarbha, South India.
When he was seven years old, he received ordination from
Rakulabhadra, the abbot of Nalanda. After studying all the texts
of the Mahayana sutra and tantra, he became a proficient and
influential scholar. With the help of the art of alchemy, he
maintained for many years five hundred bhikshus of Nalanda. He
established one hundred and eight centers of Mahayana in the one
hundred and eight temples. He built two lofty stone-pillars with
statues of the Mahakala deity on top of them . He also built a stone
wall surrounding the Vajrasana Stupa with images on the walls
and one hundred and eight stupas outside the wall. He also built
the boundary wall of the Dhanyakataka Stupa and, within this
boundary wall, he built one hundred and eight stupas.
16

A Garland of Pearls
After Acharya Nagarjuna, Acharya Aryadeva took care of the
teachings of the Buddha. He was well-versed in the Tripitaka. Under
the guidance of Acharya Nagarjuna, he attained many spiritual
accomplishments (siddhis) on the Shri Parvata Mount in South India.
He was entrusted with the substantial responsibility of the innermost
quintessential instructions of the teachings of the Buddha by Acharya
Nagarjuna before he passed away. After Acharya Nagarjuna passed
away, he worked for the welfare of numerous sentient beings in the
adjacent lands of Shri Parvata. He built twenty-four monasteries.
Durdharsakala, a non-Buddhist, arrived at Nalanda and
defeated the Buddhists in the debates. Then Acharya Aryadeva
was invited to Nalanda. There he defeated Durdharsakala in the
debate three times. Later Durdharsakala became a Buddhist and
soon became a master of the Tripitaka. He was also called by the
name Acharya Ashvagosha.
In the eastern part of India, through the Mahayoga and
Anuyoga teachings, King Jah and his disciples, Lalita-vajra,
Buddhaguhya, Sukhapraaana and Padmakara had placed countless
sentient beings into the state of Buddhahood.
In the southern part of India, many mahasiddhas such Acharya
Nagarjuna had greatly elucidated the teachings of the Buddha
through the outer and inner sections of the Secret Tantra.
In the western part of India, through the Atiyoga teachings, many
great masters such as Prahevajra, Manjushrimitra and Padmasambhava
had liberated many fortunate sentient beings.
In short, the eighty-four mahasiddhas such as Shri Saraha and
many other siddhas such as Acharya Jnanapada, Dipamkara-bhadra
and Acharya Shridhara came and liberated countless fortunate
sentient beings primarily through the Mahayana Secret Mantra.
17

A Garland of Pearls
ws
Jebang Nyernga
19

A Garland of Pearls
Guru Padmasambhava

A Garland of Pearls
The Spread of Buddhism in Tibet
There were six great regions where the Buddhadharma spread on
this earth: India, China, Tibet, Khotan, Shambhak and Kailash. If
asked when the Buddhadharma came to the Land of Snow, the
Root Tantra of Manjushri states:
After subsiding the lake in the Land of Snow,
A forest of fruit trees will appear...
As prophesied, the lake slowly subsided and a thick forest gradually
covered the region. During that time, a monkey was blessed by
the Great Compassionate One (Avalokiteshvara). From his union
with a female rock ogress the Tibetan people came into being. It is
said that initially the region was occupied by non-humans and
then gradually humans came and lived there.
Later an Indian prince, an emanation of Bodhisattva
Sarvanirvirana Viskambhi came to Tibet. He became the first king
of Tibet. He was called Nyatri Tsenpo. After him , in succession,
Tibet was ruled by the reigns of different kings: the Seven Heavenly
Thrones, the Two Celestial Space, the Six Excellences of Earth, the
Eight Groups of Space and the Five Powerful Ones.
The Immaculate Goddess Sutral2 states:
After 2,500 years of my passing into nirvana, the
sublime dharma will spread in the Land of the Red
Face.
21

A Garland of Pearls
As prophesied, the twenty-eighth king of Tibet, Lha Thothori
Nyentsen, an emanation of Bodhisattva Samantabhadra, reigned
in Tibet. When he was residing in Yumbu Lagang fortress, Pandita
Buddhirakshita and the translator Lithise came to see him and
presented the Karandavyuha Sutra. Since the King could not read
and understand its meaning he sent them back. However, he took
it as an auspicious omen even though he did not understand its
meaning. He called it a "Powerful Mystery” and worshipped it. As
a result, the sixty-one year old King became a youthful prince of
sixteen years of age. His life was prolonged by sixty years and he
lived one hundred and twenty years. It was prophesied to him
that during the fifth generation the meaning of this text would be
known. This is the beginning of the sublime dharma in Tibet.
The Manjushri Root Tantral3 states:
In the region called "Abode of the Gods”
Situated inside the snowy mountain ,
A king called “God of Humans”
Will be born in the Lichavhi lineages.
As prophesied, from Lha Thothori Nyentsen, the fifth succession
was the Dharma King Songtsen Gampo, an emanation of
Avalokiteshvara. He ascended the throne and ruled the country
when he was thirteen years old . When he was fifteen years old, his
emanation Bhikshu Akarmati brought the self-appeared statue of
Avalokiteshvara to Tibet. He instructed his minister Gartongtsen,
an emanation of Vajrapani, to bring the princesses-the Nepalese
princess Bhrikuti Devi, an emanation of Frowning (Yellow) Tara
and the Chinese princess Wengchen Kongjo, an emanation of White
Tara-to his court.
The Dharma King built Rasa Trulnang and Ramoche temples
and the Potala palace. He subdued and transformed those who
were hostile to the Buddhadharma and sentient beings. Without
fear, while sitting on the great throne, he ruled the country. He
was compassionate, brave and fearless. He displayed many
22

A Garland of Pearls
inconceivable emanations and his fame spread far and wide. The
kings of many countries such as India, China, Persia and Gesar
showed great reverence and paid tributes to him .
Since Tibet had no writing system , the Dharma King sent his
minister Thonmi Sambhota to India. Based on Indian alphabets
he created a new system of writing which was necessary for Tibetans.
The King invited many scholars from India and Buddhist monks
from China and translated numerous Buddhist texts into Tibetan.
Thus, Buddhism was introduced in Tibet.
In the past in Tibet, there were no instructions of Dharma
regarding what to adopt and discard. The Dharma King Songtsen
Gampo introduced a legal code and taught his subjects writing
and the good law such as the Ten Divine Virtues and the Sixteen
Pure Human Laws. Thus, he introduced the combined spiritual
and secular system of governance in Tibet. With his blessings, Tibet
became a source of wealth, prosperity and dharma.
From the Dharma King Songtsen Gampo, the fifth succession
was the Dharma King Trisong Deutsen, an emanation of Manjushri.
He discovered a copper-plate on which the Dharma King Songtsen
Gampo inscribed these words: “My nephew bearing my name with
the addition of the word “De' will spread the Buddhadharma."
Thinking, “ This 'De' must be me,” he ascended the throne at the
age of thirteen.
The thought of spreading Buddhadharma came into his mind
when he was twenty years old and he invited Abbot Shantirakshita
from India, who gave teachings to the King such as on the ten
virtuous actions, the eighteen elements (dhatus), etc. When Abbot
Shantirakshita was laying the foundation for Samye Monastery, all
the gods and demons of Tibet became angry and started to destroy
in the night the constructions that the humans built in the day.
There were many other obstructions too. On these pretexts, the
ministers who were hostile to Buddhadharma forced Abbot
Shantirakshita to depart to Nepal.
Seeing the King become gloomy, Abbot Shantirakshita
pronounced, “Although I am not ignorant of the Buddhist and
23

A Garland of Pearls
non -Buddhist pitakas, and am well trained in bodhichitta, I am
not capable of using wrathful force to subdue the demons and
gods. You will accomplish your goal if you invite Mahasiddha
Padmasambhava, an emanation of Buddha Amitabha, who was
born in Jambudvipa and achieved the immortal body of light.
When the Jarung Khashor Stupa (Boudhanath Stupa) was being
constructed in Nepal during the epoch of Buddha Kashyapa, you
had a connection to this Mahasiddha in terms of brotherhood and
aspiration-prayers.”
As instructed, the Dharma King sent messengers on several
occasions to invite Mahasiddha Padmasambhava. The Mahasiddha
accepted his invitation and proceeded to Tibet. On the way, he
subdued and bound all hostile and malevolent non-human forces
by oath. Some of the demons were the Twelve Guardian Goddesses,
the Thirteen Hunting Gods and the Twenty-one Genyens. He
then proceeded to Drakmar (Red Cliff) where Abbot
Shantirakshita, Mahasiddha Padmasambhava and the Dharma King
Trisong Deutsen met and they proceeded to Samye.
Abbot Shantirakshita examined and blessed the ground and
took the monastery of Odantapuri as a model and made a plan
containing the forms of Mount Sumeru at the centre, the eight
continents and sub-continents in the eight directions, all these
surrounded by a circumference of iron. It is said that it was
constructed by humans in the day and demons and gods in the
night. Hence, the temple is called Samye Mingyur Lhungyi Drubpa
(Unchanging and Spontaneously Perfected Temple of Samye). It
was completed in 814 CE. Abbot Shantirakshita and Mahasiddha
Padmasambhava consecrated the temple. Many auspicious omens
appeared and miracles happened during the rites of consecration
of the temple.
From India, one hundred and eight panditas were invited (such
as Mahapandita Vimalamitra) and they taught the art of translation
to hundreds of young Tibetans. One hundred and eight trained
translators (such as Vairocana) graduated. In the Drajor Tsangmang
Ling, the science of grammar was taught and dictionaries were
24

A Garland of Pearls
composed. Twelve bhikshus from Vikramshila Monastery were
invited to the Namdak Trimkhang Ling and three hundred Tibetans
were ordained as monks starting with the “Seven Men on Probation”
based the Mulasarvastivadin Vinaya tradition headed by Abbot
Shantirakshita. Thus, monasticism was introduced in Tibet for the
first time. In Duedul Ngagpa Ling, Padmasambhava, Vimalamitra
and others gave tantric teachings. In Dragyur Ling, Indian and
Tibetan translators translated the Tripitaka and Four Classes of
Tantra along with their commentaries into Tibetan from Sanskrit.
They also translated some texts found in Khotan and China such
as the Jewel Mound Sutra and the Huge Collection of Sutras. In Bairo
Ling and Jampel Ling, the Buddhadharma and their commentaries
were studied and discussed. In Miyo Samten Ling, the teachings
of sutra and tantra were practiced. In Semkye Ling, the bodhichitta
vows were bestowed. In Korzoe Pehar Ling, the treasures were kept.
In the Mandala of Vajradhatu, empowerments were given by tantric
masters such as Dharmakirti. By these and other similar works,
the Buddhadharma was fully and thoroughly introduced and
established in Tibet.
Thus, Abbot Shantirakshita and Acharya Padmasambhava along
with his twenty-five main disciples called “Jebang Nyernga”
translated all the sutric and tantric texts primarily found in Nalanda
and other places in India, China and Khotan. Abbot Shantirakshita
taught the Vinayapitaka and Sutrapitaka extensively. Acharya
Padmasambhava and Panchen Vimalamitra introduced the tantric
teachings and made them flourish like a waxing moon.
During that time, twelve learning centers were established in
the three provinces of Tibet where people were encouraged to study
the unique traditional values and customs, culture, ancestral
асaccounts, politics, history and grammarmar..
Especially, with miraculous powers, Padmasambhava and
Vimalamitra brought all the texts of the uncommon three cycles
of tantric teachings Mahayoga, Anuyoga and Atiyoga from the
realms of the gods, Nagas and the secret treasury of dakas and
dakinis. Through these teachings, many fortunate and destined
25

A Garland of Pearls
disciples were placed into the state of liberation, such as the twenty
five mahasidhas of Chimphu hermitage in Samye, the 107 siddhas
of Chuwori who attained the body of light, the thirty realized
yogis of Yangzong, the twenty-five dakinis who attained the body
of light and the eighty siddhas of Yerpa Mountain who attained
rainbow bodies. In this way, Padmasambhava had filled the Land
of Snow with such learned and accomplished masters.
When the glorious Atisha Dipamkara visited Tibet, he said,
“Even in India, the Buddhadharma did not spread just like it spread
during the time of the Abbot (Shantirakshita), the Acharya
(Padmasambhava) and the Dharma King (Trisong Deutsen).”
Moreover, Omniscient Mipham said:
The three ancestors brought the Buddhadharma in
this country,
The Abbot, Acharya and Dharma King hoisted the
victorious banner of Buddhadharma,
And brought together a huge assembly of Dharma
holders,
Their kindness to Tibet is incomparable.
Then in-between the Buddhadharma faced some adverse
circumstances. However, by the kindness of successive Dharma kings
and many sublime spiritual masters, the Buddhadharma has been
revived.
The Unwinking Lord(the only object of refuge and the
temporal and spiritual leader of Tibet), Kyabje Duejom Rinpoche,
Kyabje Dhilgon Khentse Rinpoche, Kyabje Drupwang Pema
Norbu Rinpoche, Kyabje Minling Trichen Rinpoche, Kyabje
Karmapa Rinpoche, Kyabje Sakya Trizin Rinpoche, Kyabje Gaden
Tripa Rinpoche, Kyabje Dodrupchen Rinpoche, Kyabje Jadrel
Rinpoche, Kyabje Taklung Tsetrul Rinpoche, Kyabje Trulshik
Rinpoche and many non-sectarian spiritual masters of Nyingma,
Kagyue, Sakya and Geluk traditions spread the Buddhadharma in
India, Nepal, Bhutan and Sikkim and in many other eastern and
26

A Garland of Pearls
western countries and led countless fortunate and destined disciples
to the state of permanent happiness.
In Tibet, Khenchen Choeje Yeshin Norbu the unmistaken
reincarnation of Terton Lerab Lingpa and his heart disciples
Khenchen Tsultrim Lodoe and Karma Kuchen of Palyul and many
other non-sectarian spiritual teachers of Nyingma, Kagyue, Sakya
and Geluk traditions established many monastic communities and
spread the precious Buddhadharma through teaching, debate and
retreat.
This is a brief history of Tibetan Buddhism , which is the only
source of all happiness and benefit in this and future lives.
27

A Garland of Pearls
A Brief History of Tolag Nenang Monastery
In the Land of Snow, the domain of Avalokiteshvara,
In the region where all walks of life earn virtues and
merits
Lies the monastery of Tolag Nenang.
Who would not enjoy composing the excellent
accounts of this monastery?
Tibet is a country where religious and secular values are
harmoniously combined and its influence rises like that of the
summer river. It is fenced by snow mountain ranges, domed by
the sky of the eight-spoke wheel, decorated with the ground of the
eight-petal lotus and embellished in its surroundings by many
marvelous symbols, such as the eight auspicious symbols.
Due to the ripening of the imprints of the wholesome deeds of
sentient beings living in this country and the aspirational prayers
of numerous great noble beings, countless emanations of buddhas
and bodhisattvas came to protect and guide them .
Tibet is divided into three regions: Three Regions of Ngari of
upper Tibet, Four Rulags of Ü and Tsang of middle Tibet and Six
Gangs of Dokham of lower Tibet. Tolag Nenang Monastery is
situated near the Pashoe district, in Tshawa Gang, one of the Six
Gangs. This monastery holds the long-standing tradition of Gyalwa
Palyul Namgyal Changchup Choeling Monastery.
Through miracles Guru Padmasambhava, the Second Buddha,
visited and blessed this place. On top of this holy place, there are
29

A Garland of Pearls
various different cliffs. There are many beautiful self-appeared
caves perfect places for meditation amongst the cliffs. There are
also numerous self-appeared images such as a footprint of
Shakyamuni Buddha when he was seven years old, the thousand
armed and thousand-eyed Avalokiteshvara, Manjushri, Tara, Guru
Rinpoche, a stupa of enlightenment, a white dharma conch shell,
mantras of Guru Rinpoche and the six-syllable mantra of
Avalokiteshvara.
Many great non-sectarian spiritual masters, such as Phagpa
Thongwa Dhonden and the Eleventh Karmapa, have visited and
blessed this place. Every year tens of thousands of people of all
walks of life from various places visit this place for pilgrimage. The
pilgrims become speechless over the marvels of this holy place and
feel like never leaving. It is said that anyone, whether devoted or
not, will generate devotion and tears will fall from their eyes when
they behold this holy place. It is known to have a hugely
empowering energy.
In 1808 the Great Tertön14 Do Dhargang Choekyi Dorjee
visited this beautiful site and founded a monastery, erected
representations of Buddha's body, speech and mind and set up a
monastic learning centre. It is called To-lag Ne-nang Nga-gyur
Do-ngag Rig-pae Gat-tshel Ling.15 He was one of the many
accomplished spiritual masters of Gyalwa Palyul Namgyal
Changchup Choeling Monastery. He was a well-known tertön who
found confidence in the teachings of sutra and tantra and attained
incomparable magical powers.
His reincarnation was Tulku Karma Gyaltsen. It was prophesied:
"At Taklung Tsobu, in the monastic learning centre of the Karma
Khagyu tradition, he will be called Karma Gyaltsen...” His
reincarnation was Sangye Yeshi Rinpoche who was the supreme
head of the Jang Tana Monastery. Both of them worked hard for
the benefit of sentient beings and the teachings of the Buddha.
In 1959, by ripening the seeds of the common black-karma of
the Tibetan people, the “circumstantial cyclone' uprooted the
country, along with its secular and spiritual values. At that time,
30

A Garland of Pearls
this monastery also suffered destruction. However, by the light of
virtuous actions, it still exists to some degree.
Here I write a short biography of Kyabje Netrul Sonam
Gyaltsen Rinpoche who was the fourth Great Tertön Do Dhargang
Choekyi Dorjee. Of course, I cannot write all the marvelous deeds
of this great master, just some common accounts that appear to us.
By the power of the merits earned by sentient beings, like a
cluster of stars in the sky, countless emanations of buddhas and
bodhisattvas such as Manjushri, Avalokiteshvara and Vajrapani,
Abbot Shantirakshita, Acharya Padmasambhava and Dharma King
Tritsong Deutsen appeared in Tibet and protected and guided
countless sentient beings to the ultimate happiness. Likewise, by
the prayers and aspiration of Great Tertön Do Dhargang Choekyi
Dorjee and by the force of people's special connection to him , he
took birth in the family called Lage at Tshawa Gang in the Iron
Horse year of the Tibetan calendar; 1950.
He was born with numerous auspicious signs and omens. His
father's name is Abu and his mother's name is Kunsang Choedon.
During his childhood, all the actions of his body, speech and mind
were clearly set for the benefit of sentient beings. He was gifted
with great faith in the dharma. Hence, everyone praised him by
saying, “He seems to be a reincarnation of an authentic
practitioner.” By the age of eight, he learned writing and reading
without much effort. At twelve, he received the Mind-Instructions
of the Great Perfection and the Preliminary Instructions of the Heart
Essence from Kyabje Lama Gya Tulku.
While he was completing a hundred thousand prostrations as
a preliminary practice, under a tree near his residence for days and
nights, a number of marks of accomplishment appeared. His
spiritual master and people around him were overjoyed. On
completing five hundred thousand prostrations, all the marks of
accomplishment appeared in his dreams. All the virtues of the
path , such as devotion to spiritual masters, compassion for sentient
beings and a pure outlook towards the dharma appeared to him
effortlessly.
31

A Garland of Pearls
When he reached the age of twenty-seven, he set forth to Lhasa
and studied under many spiritual masters of both old and new
traditions of Tibet, such as Kushab Majin. Then he stayed at Ütse
of the Sera Monastery in retreat for three years and three months.
His main practice was on Hayagriva and Vajra-kilaya deities. He
clearly saw all the marks of accomplishment. The great practitioner
experienced the emptiness of the union processes of Generation
and Perfection. The experiences are as follows. The experience of
movement is like a waterfall. The experience of attainment is like a
river flowing in a gorge. The experience of familiarity is like the
gentle flow of a river in the plains. The experience of steadiness is
like a pond undulating under a breeze and the experience of
perfection is like the great ocean free from waves.
Over time, as the karmic connection ripened he returned to
his native place. At the age of thirty-one, he was recognized as the
reincarnation of Great Tertön Do Dhargang Choekyi Dorjee by
Laekyi Wangmo Namgyal Dolma, the dakini of Yago region and
enthroned in Tolag Nenang Monastery.
Then, from Jadrel Lama Chime Rigzin, he received instructions
on Chö practices from the text Precious Garland of Collection of
Chö Practices, instructions on Phowa practices and many other
instructions and empowerments. From Palyul Tulku Karma
Kuchen, Gyangkhang Tulku and Tertön Khenrab Woser, he received
Jamgön Kongtrül Lodrö Thaye's Treasure Trove of Precious Hidden
Teachings (Rinchen Terdző) and many other pith instructions.
It is stated in one of the sutras:
If one finds complete confidence in the meaning of
reality
Hundreds of thousands of Dharma treasures overflow
from the mind.
As stated, even during the dark ages when there were no teachings
of the Sutra, he worked unceasingly and extensively to hold, preserve
and spread the teachings of the Secret Mantra and to free those
who were difficult to tame.
32

A Garland of Pearls
In 1980, he got permission from the higher authorities and
reconstructed a new Tolag Nenang Monastery. Inside the perfectly
adorned prayer hall, he erected a replica of the famous statue of
Jowo Shakyamuni Buddha in the Lhasa Jokang, as the main
representation of the body of the Buddha. He further erected a
statue of Padmasambhava Nangsi Zilnön made from copper gilded
with gold, a statue of Khadro Yeshi Tsogyal to his right and a
statue of Lhacham Mandarava to his left, statues adorned with
gold such as Vajrasattva, Tara, Amitabha and four-armed
Avalokiteshvara, one hundred statues of peaceful and wrathful
deities, the statues of the Six Ornaments and Two Excellences,
statues of the Buddha performing the twelve deeds, a statue of
thousand-armed and thousand-eyed Avalokiteshvara, one thousand
statues of Amitabha and a scroll painting of a thousand buddhas.
As for the representations of the speech of the Buddha, he
kept 108 volumes of Kangyur and 225 volumes of Tengyur, the
volumes of Rinchen Terdzo and many other sacred texts written by
the Indian and Tibetan scholars along with their secular works. He
restarted the traditional rites and rituals at the monastery. Later,
he established a meditation center. Gradually, he erected fifteen
huge prayer-wheels (containing a hundred million six -syllable
mantras) and about one thousand small prayer-wheels.
As for the representations of the mind of the Buddha, he erected
three Jangchub (bodhi) stupas.
In these and other ways, he was able to establish and continue
the Kama and Terma teaching traditions.16 There were about eighty
monks at the monastery. Gradually, he had countless fortunate
disciples from Tibet, Nepal and India.
Furthermore, he saved many lives of human beings who were
about to die of sickness etc. and freed many lives of animals in the
nick of time from being killed.
Kyabje Dujom Jigdel Yeshi Dorjee said:
Though one may know the ultimate reality of
emptiness explained in sutras and tantras,
33

A Garland of Pearls
They may not have properly understood emptiness
as their minds are stiff like horns!
As stated, he often advises his disciples, “Practice dharma according
to dharma, otherwise, it will become the cause of your downfall in
the lower realms.”
Moreover, since he found an unshakable confidence in the
practice of what to adopt and what to reject, numerous marks of
accomplishment appeared. Although this wise saint is inseparable
from Mahaguru Padmasambhava, at present he is our protector,
object of refuge and last resort. At present this great saint the axle
of the teachings of Vajragarbha-lives in Tibet with perfect health .
The excellent buddha came to this world
Hoisted the victorious banners in the four directions
The hero opened hundreds of doors to the teachings
of the Buddha.
May this gracious spiritual master live forever!
Here is a brief account of the holy place of Nenang region based
on the oral descriptions made by this great spiritual master:
“ This is a self-appeared image of Lama Shri Singha, the root spiritual
master of Ugen Rinpoche (Padmasambhava). This one to the left
is a self-appeared image of Ushnisha Vijaya deity. If men and
women, who cannot bring forth children, prostrate and
circumambulate this image with faith , they can give birth. It also
helps to heal many kinds of disease. This is the hundred-syllable
mantra of Vajrasattva deity. All these small stones are also self
appeared. This painting is not man -made either. Look! It appears
as if it is painted with white butter. If you look carefully, you can
see and also touch many self-appeared images of deities, and mantras
such as the six-syllable mantra and the hundred-syllable mantra
on these small stones. On all these small stones, there are countless
self-appeared images of deities and mantra syllables.”

A Garland of Pearls
Without engraving on the piles of stones,
Naturally appeared hundreds of dazzling major and
minor marks of a buddha,
Such magnificent images of buddhas are
incomparable!
Thus, the lord of immortality explained.
“ These images initially appear in grey-colored form . Later deities
appear from them . Some of the images of deities arise only after
the appearance of thrones. Some images come forth from
underground. If people walk through these places, there is a risk of
stepping over these images. Hence, pilgrims should pay attention
not to step over them . The self-appeared images to the left are one
thousand images of Amitabha, and the rest of them are the images
of bodhisattvas."
When seeing these harmonious manifestations
Everyone receives the nectar of joy.
The joy of seeing buddhas in person
Is no greater than seeing these physical images of
buddhas.

faith in these images the benefit is enormous.”

A Garland of Pearls
The Benefits of the Six -Syllable Mantra
It is said that the Land of Snow is the abode of Avalokiteshvara. OM
MANI PADME HUM is the six-syllable mantra of Avalokiteshvara,
which is the paramount teaching that he gave. Many of these six
syllable mantras spontaneously appeared in the mountains to make
the devoted feel more confident in his teachings.
The benefits of the six-syllable mantra are mentioned in the
hagiography of Guru Padmasambhava entitled Zang-ling-ma:17
The benefits of the sacred syllables OM MANI PADME
HUM are: OM pacifies the suffering of the transmigration
and downfall of the gods and helps them attain happiness,
MA pacifies the suffering of the conflict of the demigods
(asuras) and helps them attain happiness, NI pacifies the
suffering of birth, aging, sickness and death, constant toil
and misfortunes of humans and accomplishes happiness.
PAD pacifies the suffering of stupidity of the animals and
accomplishes happiness, ME pacifies the suffering of hunger
and thirst of the hungry-ghosts (pretas) and accomplishes
happiness, and HUM pacifies the suffering of heat and
cold of the hell beings and accomplishes happiness.
Moreover, the Sutra Showing the Complete Names of the Buddhas18
states:
Just by hearing the name of Arya Avalokiteshvara, one
will be protected from all faults of this life and attain the

A Garland of Pearls
unsurpassable state of perfectly complete
enlightenment in the next life.
The Ratnakaranda Sutra states:
If this six -syllable mantra is painted or written on cliffs
and walls and touched and looked at, and if they are
glimpsed by men and women, boys and girls, they will
become bodhisattvas of the final stage.
As mentioned, just by meditating one time on Arya Avalokiteshvara,
just by hearing the name once, just by reciting the six-syllable mantra
once and just by seeing and touching the painted six -syllable mantra,
one will be protected from the human and non-human fears such as
rahula spirits, maras, vicious animals, sicknesses and negative
influences and one's wishes for this life (such as long life, wealth and
power) will be accomplished and one's heaviest karmic actions done
in past lives (such as the five heinous deeds) will be purified and
successively one will be born into the happy realms.
42

A Garland of Pearls
The Benefits of Prostration
and Circumambulation
The holy places (mentioned in chapter 4) are equivalent to Tsari Pema
Kö in North-east India, Mount Phayul near Zayul and Khawa Karpo
of Gyalmo Tsawa Rong. It seems that these holy places are the actual
holy places of Khawa Karpo because the Dakini's Guidebook to Holy
Placesl' states:
The benefit of making thirteen circumambulations
around these holy places is equal to making one
circumambulation around Khawa Karpo.
Thus, as the saying goes, “Relics will appear from the tooth of a dog
if one has faith”. It is very important to have faith and pure perception
without differentiating between whether it is authentic or not. It is so
because a sutra states:
All phenomena are circumstantial
As they depend entirely on one's aspiration.
Whatever aspirational prayer one makes,
It will become as prayed .
In brief, the virtues and merits earned by those who make offerings in
the vast and open regions from Vajrasana, the centre of Magadha, to
the coastal areas of the vast oceans are impossible to express in words.
Ema! How wonderful!
If merits earned from one hundred puja offerings
43

A Garland of Pearls
Can swiftly attain the state of immortality,
Who can measure the merits earned by making infinite
offerings
To the excellent and unparalleled holy places of this
earth?
Moreover, if one prostrates and circumambulates with pure
motivation, one posits seeds of an equal number to the prostrations
and circumambulations of becoming a bodhisattva of the tenth ground
(bhumi) and attaining the omniscient wisdom of a buddha.
The most holy places, such as Vajrasana of India and the secret
treasury of dakinis of Odiyana, are not greater than these holy
places (mentioned in chapter 4]. Hence, if one prostrates,
circumambulates and makes offerings to these holy places, one
will earn equal virtues and merits of prostration, circumambulation
and offerings made to the most holy places of India and Odiyana.

A Garland of Pearls
Epilogue
I have composed this book by collecting some elegant teachings and
I confess before the buddhas and bodhisattvas and ask for forgiveness
if I have written anything that contradicts their thoughts. If there are
any virtues and merits gained by composing this book, by the power
of its virtue may the teachings of Buddhadharma in general, and the
Dzongchen teachings of the Nyingma tradition in particular, flourish
and last forever. May all the non-sectarian spiritual masters who hold
these teachings live forever and may their enlightened activities pervade
like the expanse of space.
It is said:
The only source of benefit and happiness
May the Buddhadharma last for a long time!
And may the victory banner of the lifespan
Of all the holders of the Buddhadharma exist eternally!
As stated, to uphold, preserve and spread the sublime Buddhadharma,
a sangha community who live a pure life is needed, thereby rainfalls
come in time, harvests become abundant and cattle become healthy,
and all sentient beings enjoy perfect happiness.
May the sangha community and the whole population of this
world pacify their obstacles and live in freedom and peace.
With these prayers, I, Pema Choephel, have completed this
book on October 5, 2008 at Ngagyur Nyingma Palyul Shedra
Choekhor Ling College in Bir, Himachal Pradesh , India.
45

A Garland of Pearls
Colophon
By relying upon the profound instructions of the wise
I, a logician, tried to compose this work.
Before the community of knowledgeable and learned ones
I confess my ignorance, contradictions, mistakes and faults.
By the continuum of the rain of virtue and merit of this
composition
May the entire fertile soil of Buddhadharma, the source of all
happiness and benefit,
Flourish with the harvest of the fruits of secret mantra
And may all sentient beings enjoy the perfect spiritual life.
May all sentient beings including my parents of this life
Purify their two obscurations and complete their two
accumulations
Generate the two bodhichittas in their minds
And swiftly attain the state of the two bodies of a buddha.
Although I was encouraged time and again by my spiritual master,
Sonam Gyaltsen Rinpoche (who is in Tibet) and many of my dharma
friends to write a brief account of Tolag Nyenang Monastery which
enthralls many devoted people, I could not do so. This was because
firstly, I was lost in an unknown and uncertain place for a long time.
Secondly, I am not gifted with intelligence by birth. Thirdly, I am not
knowledgeable although I have studied the profound Buddhadharma
diligently since childhood. However, by the instruction of my spiritual
master and inspiration from my dharma friends, I have joyfully
composed a drop from the vast ocean by collecting information from
numerous scriptural texts.

I was born in the Og-leg family near Tsawa Gang in the Dokham
province in 1980. I was named Pema Choephel. Under the loving
care of my parents, I started to learn how to read and write Tibetan
in 1990.I feel that this is the best gift I have received from my parents. In
1995, as per my parents' wishes, I was ordained as a monk in the Tolag
Nenang Monastery. Gradually, I learned the rites and rituals, and how to play
our monastery's religious musical instruments. Then for five years, I served
my spiritual master as a personal attendant. With the force of my karma that
I had accumulated in past lives, I had a strong faith and conviction in the
Buddhadharma and always wanted to study. After facing numerous challenges
and hardships during my journey from Tibet, I reached India in 1999. Then
for nine years, I had the opportunity to study Buddhadharma in Ngagyur
Nyingma Palyul Shedra Choekhor Ling College in Bir, Himachal Pradesh, India.
I always aspire to work for the benefit of others in future. Hence, I continue
to pursue my studies by listening and contemplating, teaching and debating
with full commitment and diligence.
